Dear Ms. Moses,
The settlement demand that follows, as well as the medical records and bills, is presented to 
resolve our client’s claim. We understand your company relies on computer software programs 
to evaluate personal injury claims. This settlement is designed and organized specifically for the 
purpose of making the evaluation as effective as possible.
All the value drivers and factors presented in the demand were taken directly from the medical 
records and bills. The injuries and damages are submitted based on our knowledge and 
understanding of our client's history and expected future losses. We reserve the right to amend 
this demand at any time in the future to accurately reflect our client's situation.

History of Present iliness
The patient presents following motor vehicle collision and Patient presents emergency department after an MVC that occurred approximately 1500 on
1/24/2024. Patient was driving on street, approximately 35 mph and a vehicle was backing out of the drive and struck his passenger side. The patient
struck his head on the side window of the temporal region. He has had a severe headache since then. He has had some slight nausea but no vomiting,
no loss of balance or fails. Patient denies any loss of consciousness. He was wearing his seatbelt and no airbags were deployed. He complains of
some sternal chest wall pain. He is AxOx4.. The onset was 1500 yesterday. The Collision was passenger side impact and moderate speed. The
patient was the driver. There were safety mechanisms including seat belt, no airbag. neck, left head (temporal region), chest wall. The degree of pain is
severe and 8/10. . The degree of bleeding is none. Risk factors consist of none. The patient's dominant hand is the right hand. Therapy today: none.
Associated symptoms: nausea and chest wall pain, headache.

Differential Diagnosis: Motor vehicle collision, head injury, cervical spine injury, contusion.
Rationale: Patient presents emergency department after an MVC that occurred approximately 1500 on 1/24/2024. Patient was driving on street,
approximately 35 mph and a vehicle was backing out of the drive and struck his passenger side. The patient struck his head an the
side window of the temporal region. He has had a severe headache since then. He has had some slight nausea but no vomiting, no
loss of balance or falls. Patient denies any loss of consciousness. He was wearing his seatbelt and no airbags were deployed. He
complains of some sternal chest wall pain. He is AxOx4. Will perform scan of his head, neck and an x-ray of his chest. He is agreeable
with this treatment plan..

Education Materials
Chest Contusion, Adult
A chest contusion is a deep bruise on the chest. Bruises happen when an injury causes bleeding under the skin. Minor bruises may
cause no pain, but serious ones may stay painful and swollen for a few weeks.
What are the causes?
. Motor vehicle crashes.
. Fails.
. Bicycle injuries.
. Injuries from playing contact sports.
What increases the risk?
. Playing sports in which contact and falls are common.
What are the signs or symptoms?
+ Swelling in the chest.
. Pain and tenderness in your chest.
. Pain when you move your chest or your shoulders.

Emergency
. Redness in the chest. The area may also turn blue, purple, or yellow.
. Pain when you take deep breaths.
How is this treated?
. Rest.
. Put ice to the injured area.
. Do deep-breathing exercises. This reduces the risk of pneumonia.
+ Take over-the-counter medicines to treat pain.
. You may be given oxygen if:
—46 You have trouble breathing.
—46 You have low oxygen levels.
Follow these instructions at home:
Managing pain, stiffness, and swelling
* If you are told, put ice on the injured area. To do this:
—46 Put ice in a plastic bag.
—46 Place a towel between your skin and the bag.
—46 Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2-3 times per day.
—46 Take off the ice if your skin turns bright red. This is very important. If you cannot feel pain, heat, or cold, you have a
greater risk of damage to the area.
+ Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your doctor.
General instructions
. Do not lift anything that is heavier than 10 ib (4.5 kg), or the limit that you are told.
. Rest as told by your doctor.
—46 Get up to take short walks every 1-2 hours. This is important to improve blood flow and breathing.
—46 Ask for help if you feel weak or unsteady.
. Do exercises to help with breathing, if your doctor tells you to do so.
. Do not smoke or use any products that contain nicotine or tobacco. If you need help quitting, ask your doctor.
. Keep all follow-up visits. This is important.
Contact a doctor if:

. Treatment or medicines do not help your swelling or pain.
. You have more bruising.
+ You have more swelling.
+ Your pain gets worse.
. Your symptoms do not get better in one week.
Get help right away if:
. You suddenly have a fot more pain.
. You have trouble breathing.
. You feel dizzy or weak.
. You faint.
. You have blood in your pee (urine) or poop (stool).
. You cough up biood or you vomit blood.
These symptoms may be an emergency. Get heip right away. Call your local emergency services (911 in the U.S.).
. Do not wait to see if the symptoms will go away.
. Do not drive yourself to the hospital.
Summary
. A chest contusion is a deep bruise on the chest. Bruises happen when an injury causes bleeding under the skin.
. Treatment may include resting and putting ice on the injured area.
+ Contact a doctor if treatment or medicines do not help, or if you have more pain or swelling.
. Get help right away if you suddenly have a lot of pain, or have trouble breathing, or feel weak or dizzy.
. Get help right away if you cough up blood, or if you see blood in your urine, poop, or vomit.
This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss any questions you
have with your health care provider.

Emergency
There are many types of head injuries. They can be as minor as a small bump. Some head injuries can be worse. Worse injuries
include:
.
.
Most problems from a head injury come in the first 24 hours. However, you may still have side effects up to 7-10 days after your injury. it
is important to watch your condition for any changes. You may need to be watched in the emergency department or urgent care, or you
A strong hit to the head that shakes the brain back and forth, causing damage (concussion).
A bruise (contusion) of the brain. This means there is bleeding in the brain that can cause swelling.
A cracked skull (skull fracture).
Bleeding in the brain that gathers, gets thick (makes a clot}, and forms a bump (hematoma).
may need to stay in the hospital.
What are the causes?
There are many possible causes of a head injury. A serious head injury may be caused by:
A car accident.
Bicycle or motorcycle accidents.
Sports injuries.
Fails.
Being hit by an object.
What are the signs or symptoms?
Symptoms of a head injury include a bruise, bump, or bleeding where the injury happened. Other physical symptoms may include:
Headache.
Feeling like you may vomit (nauseous) or vomiting.
Dizziness.
Blurred or double vision.
Being uncomfortable around bright lights or loud noises.
Shaking movements that you cannot control (seizures).
Feeling tired.
Trouble being woken up.
Fainting or loss of consciousness.
Mental or emotional symptoms may include:
Feeling grumpy or cranky.
Confusion and memory problems.
Having trouble paying attention or concentrating.
Changes in eating or sleeping habits.
Feeling worried or nervous (anxious).
Feeling sad (depressed).
How is this treated?

UofL Physicians 3/95/2024 11:15:18 AM PAGE 25/095 Fax server
MEH Mary & Elizabeth Hospital
Patient: FINLEY JR.,CECIL LEE DOB/Age/Sex: 7/3/1985 38 years Maile
MRN: —V001068010 Account #: [PHONE-107]
Emergency
Treatment for this condition depends on how severe the injury is and the type of injury you have. The main goal is to prevent problems
and to allow the brain time to heal.
Mild head injury
If you have a mild head injury, you may be sent home, and treatment may include:
Being watched. A responsible adult should stay with you for 24 hours after your injury and check on you often.
Physical rest.
Brain rest.
Pain medicines.
Severe head injury
If you have a severe head injury, treatment may include:
Being watched closely. This includes staying in the hospital.
Medicines to:
—46 Help with pain.
—46 Prevent seizures.
—46 Help with brain swelling.
Protecting your airway and using a machine that helps you breathe (ventilator).
Treatments to waich for and manage swelling inside the brain.
Brain surgery. This may be needed to:
—46 Remove a collection of blood or blood clots.
—46 Stop the bieeding.
—46 Remove a part of the skull. This allows room for the brain to swell.
Follow these instructions at home:
Activity
Rest.
Avoid activities that are hard or tiring.
Make sure you get enough sleep.
Let your brain rest. Do this by limiting activities that need a lot of thought or attention, such as:
—46 Watching TV.
—46 Playing memory games and puzzles.
—46 Job-related work or homework.
—46 Working on the computer, social media, and texting.
Avoid activities that could cause another head injury until your doctor says it is okay. This includes playing sports. Having
another head injury, especiaily before the first one has healed, can be dangerous.
Ask your doctor when it is safe for you to go back to your normal activities, such as work or school. Ask your doctor for a
step-by-step plan for slowly going back to your normal activities.
Ask your doctor when you can drive, ride a bicycle, or use heavy machinery. Do not do these activities if you are dizzy.
Lifestyle

Emergency
. Do not drink alcohol until your doctor says it is okay.
. Do not use drugs.
. If it is harder than usual to remember things, write them down.
. If you are easily distracted, try to do one thing at a time.
+ Talk with family members or close friends when making important decisions.
+ Tell your friends, family, a trusted co-worker, and work manager about your injury, symptoms, and limits (restrictions). Have
them watch for any problems that are new or getting worse.
General instructions
. Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your doctor.
. Have someone stay with you for 24 hours after your head injury. This person should watch you for any changes in your
symptoms and be ready to get help.
. Keep all follow-up visits as told by your doctor. This is important.
How is this prevented?
+ Work on your balance and strength. This can help you avoid falls.
. Wear a seat belt when you are in a moving vehicie.
. Wear a helmet when you:
—46 Ride a bicycle.
—46 Ski.
—46 Do any other sport or activity that has a risk of injury.
. If you drink alcohol:
—46 Limit how much you use to:
—52 0~1 drink a day for nonpregnant women.
-52 0-2 drinks a day for men.
—46 Be aware of how much alcohol is in your drink. In the U.S., one drink equals one 12 oz boitle of beer (355 mL), one 5
oz glass of wine (148 mL), or one 1/2 oz glass of hard liquor (44 mL).
+ Make your home safer by:
—46 Getting rid of clutter from the floors and stairs. This includes things that can make you trip.
—46 Using grab bars in bathrooms and handrails by stairs.
—46 Placing non-slip mats on floors and in bathtubs.
—46 Putting more light in dim areas.

+ Centers for Disease Control and Prevention: www.cdc.gov
Get help right away if:
. You have:
—46 A very bad headache that is not helped by medicine.
—46 Trouble walking or weakness in your arms and legs.
—46 Clear or bloody fluid coming from your nose or ears.
—46 Changes in how you see (vision).
—46 A seizure.
—46 More confusion or more grumpy moods.
+ Your symptoms get worse.
. You are sleepier than normal and have trouble staying awake.
. You lose your balance.
+ The black centers of your eyes (pupils) change in size.
. Your speech is slurred,
. Your dizziness gets worse.
. You vomit.
These symptoms may be an emergency. Do not wait to see if the symptoms will go away. Get medical heip right away. Call
your local emergency services (911 in the U.S.). Do not drive yourself to the hospital.
Summary
. Head injuries can be as minor as a small bump. Some head injuries can be worse.
+ Treatment for this condition depends on how severe the injury is and the type of injury you have.
. Have someone stay with you for 24 hours after your head injury.
. Ask your doctor when it is safe for you to go back to your normal activities, such as work or school.
+ To prevent a head injury, wear a seat belt in a car, wear a helmet when you usea bicycle, limit your alcohol use, and make
your home safer.
This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss any questions you
have with your health care provider.
Document Revised: [DOB-54] Document Reviewed: [DOB-55] Elsevier Patient Education © 2023 Elsevier inc.
Cervical Sprain
A cervical sprain is also called a neck sprain. It is a stretch or tear in one or more ligaments in the neck. Ligaments are tissues that
connect bones to each other.
Neck sprains can be mild, bad, or very bad. A very bad sprain in the neck can cause the bones in the neck to be unstable. This can
damage the spinal cord. lt can also cause serious problems in the brain, spinal cord, and nerves (nervous system).
Most neck sprains heal in 4—6 weeks. It can take more or less time depending on:
. What caused the injury.
. The amount of injury.

Emergency
What are the causes?
Neck sprains may be caused by trauma, such as:
. An injury from an accident in a vehicle such as a car or boat.
. A fall.
+ The head and neck being moved front to back or side to side all of a sudden (whiplash injury).
Mild neck sprains may be caused by wear and tear over time.
What increases the risk?
The following factors may make you more likely to develop this condition:
+ Taking part in activities that put you at high risk of hurting your neck. These include:
—46 Contact sports.
—46 Car racing.
—46 Gymnastics.
—46 Diving.
+ Taking risks when driving or riding in a vehicle such as a car or boat.
. Arthritis caused by wear and tear of the joints in the spine.
. The neck not being very strong or flexible.
. Having had a neck injury in the past.
. Poor posture.
. Spending alot of time in certain positions that put stress on the neck. This may be from sitting at a computer for a long time.
What are the signs or symptoms?
Symptoms of this condition include:
. Your neck, shoulders, or upper back feeling:
—46 Painful or sore.
—46 Stiff.
—46 Tender.
—46 Swollen.
—46 Hot, or like it is burning.
. Sudden tightening of neck muscles (spasms).
. Not being able to move the neck very much.
. Headache.
. Feeling dizzy.
. Feeling like you may vomit, or vomiting.
. Having a hand or arm that:
—46 Feels weak.
—46 Loses feeling (feels numb).
—46 Tingles.

Emergency
You may get symptoms right away after injury, or you may get them over a few days. In some cases, symptoms may go away with
treatment and come back over time.
How is this treated?
This condition is treated by:
. Resting your neck.
. Icing the part of your neck that is hurt.
. Doing exercises to restore movement and strength to your neck (physical therapy).
If there is no swelling, you may use heat therapy 2-3 days after the injury took place. ff your injury is very bad, treatment may also
include:
. Keeping your neck in place for a length of time. This may be done using:
—46 A neck collar. This supports your chin and the back of your head.
—46 A cervical traction device. This is a sling that holds up your head. The sling removes weight and pressure from your
neck. It may also help to relieve pain.
+ Medicines that help with:
—46 Pain.
—46 irritation and swelling (inflammation).
. Medicines that help to relax your muscles (muscle relaxants).
. Surgery. This is rare.
Follow these instructions at home:
Medicines
+ Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your doctor.
. Ask your doctor if the medicine prescribed to you:
—46 Requires you to avoid driving or using heavy machinery.
—46 Can cause trouble pooping (constipation). You may need to take these actions to prevent or treat trouble pooping:
-52 Drink enough fluid to keep your pee (urine) pale yellow.
~-52 Take over-the-counter or prescription medicines.
—52 Eat foods that are high in fiber. These include beans, whole grains, and fresh fruits and vegetables.
~52 Limit foods that are high in fat and sugar. These include fried or sweet foods.
lf you have a neck collar:
. Wear it as told by your doctor. Do not take it off unless told.
. Ask your doctor before adjusting your collar.
. If you have long hair, keep it outside of the collar.
. Ask your doctor if you may take off the collar for cleaning and bathing. If you may take off the collar:

General instructions
. Do not use any products that contain nicotine or tobacco, such as cigarettes, e-cigarettes, and chewing tobacco. These can
delay healing. if you need help quitting, ask your doctor.
. Keep all follow-up visits as told by your doctor or physical therapist. This is important.
How is this prevented?
To prevent a neck sprain from happening again:
. Practice good posture. Adjust your workstation to heip you do this.
. Exercise regularly as toid by your doctor or physical therapist.
. Avoid activities that are risky or may cause a neck sprain.
Contact a doctor if:
+ Your symptoms get worse.
. Your symptoms do not get better after 2 weeks of treatment.
. Your pain gets worse.
+ Medicine does not help your pain.
. You have new symptoms that you cannot explain.
. Your neck collar gives you sores on your skin or bothers your skin.
Get heip right away if:
. You have very bad pain.
. You get any of the following in any part of your body:
—46 Loss of feeling.
—46 Tingling.
—46 Weakness.
+ You cannot move a part of your body.
. You have neck pain and either of these:
—46 Very bad dizziness.
—46 A very bad headache.
Summary
+ Acervical sprain is also called a neck sprain. It is a stretch or tear in one or more ligaments in the neck. Ligaments are tissues
that connect bones.
. Neck sprains may be caused by trauma, such as an injury ora fall.
. You may get symptoms right away after injury, or you may get them over a few days.
. Neck sprains may be treated with rest, heat, ice, medicines, exercise, and surgery.
This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss any questions you
have with your health care provider.

Emergency Awareness and Preventative Care
STROKE is an EMERGENCY
Every Minute Counts
Act FASTand Check for these signs:
FACE Does the face look uneven?
ARM Does one arm drift down?
SPEECH Does their speech sound
strange?
TIME Call 9-1-1 at any sign of stroke
Stroke Risk Factors
Atrial Fibrillation . Family history of
{irregular heartbeat) Diabetes stroke

Physical inactivity High Cholesterol .
9 and obesity
Smoking
Cigarette Smoking
The facts are clear, cigarette smoking will shorten your life. Smoking can cause many illnesses along the way. As a healthcare provider,
we recommend that you stop smoking. Assistance with quitting is available by contacting 1-800-QUIT-NOW. This is a free resource
providing counseling, support, and referral. Or you may contact your personal physician.
988 Suicide & Crisis Lifeline: 988
The 988 Suicide & Crisis Lifeline is a national network of local crisis centers that provides free and confidential emotional support to
people in suicidal crisis or emotional distress 24 hours a day, 7 days a week.
Don't Wait! Stop a Heart Attack Before it Starts
What is a heart attack?
A heart attack is damage or death to a part of the heart from severely decreased or lack of blood flow to the heart. Over time, arteries
can become narrow from the buildup of fat and cholesterol, which is called plaque. The plaque can rupture causing a blood clot to form.
When the blood clot forms, the artery can become severely narrowed or completely blocked, causing a heart attack.
+ Heart attack is the leading cause of death in the United States.
+ 85% of muscle damage occurs within the first 2 hours.
+ Delay in the recognition of heart attack symptoms increases the chances of death.
Know the early symptoms of a heart attack:

There are unusual signs of heart attack, too!
Women, the elderly, and diabetics may present with atypical symptoms:
+ Fainting/dizziness
+ Weakness
+ Confusion
Risk Factors for a Heart Attack
Some heart disease risk factors, such as age and family, cannot be changed. Others, like smoking and lack of exercise, can be
changed.
Smoking High Cholesterol Blood Pressure
Family History Obesity Age
Gender (Males are
at higher risk) Lack of Exercise Diabetes
Di Excessive Alcohol iet Stress Intake
If you or someone you know is experiencing the signs and symptoms of a heart attack, DON'T DELAY.
Cail 9-1-1 immediately and seek help.
If someone collapses, perform CPR!
Do not attempt to drive if you are having symptoms of heart attack.
Why Hands-Only CPR?
+ Hands-Only CPRhas been shown to be as effective as conventional CPRfor cardiac arrests that occur outside of a hospital.
+ Survival depends on immediately receiving CPR from someone nearby.
How do you perform Hands-Only CPR?
There are two easy steps:
+ 1. Call 9-1-1 if you see a teen or adult collapse
+ 2. Push hard and fast in the center of the chest at a beat of 100 beats per minute
Save a life!

4 WAYS TO GET AHEAD OF SEPSIS
SEPSIS is a MEDICAL EMERGENCY. Time Matters!
Infections put you and your family at risk for a life-threatening condition cailed sepsis.
« Sepsis is the body's extreme response to an infection. itis life-threatening, and without timely treatment, sepsis can rapidly lead
to tissue damage, organ failure, and death. Sepsis happens when an infection you already have-in your skin, lungs, urinary tract
or somewhere else-riggers a chain reaction throughout your body.
Take good care of
chronic conditions.
PREVENT Talk to your doctor
INFECTIONS about getting the
recommended
vaccines.
Wash your hands
frequently.
PRACTICE GOOD Keep cuts or open
HYGIENE sores clean and
covered until they
are healed.
.
Confusion or
disorientation
Shortness of breath
High heart rate
KNOW THE Fever, shivering, or
SYMPTOMS feeling very cold
Extreme pain or
discomfort
Clammy or sweaty
skin
Get medical care
IMMEDIATELY if
you suspect sepsis
4 ACT FAST or if you have an
infection that is not
getting better or is
getting worse.
To learn more about sepsis and how to prevent infections, visit www.cdc.gov/sepsis.

The examination and treatment you have received in the Emergency Department has been done to provide an appropriate evaluation
and stabilizing treatment on an emergency basis only. Given the limited resources, it is not meant to be a substitute for complete
medical care. The follow-up provider you named will receive a copy of your records and all test reports. IT IS IMPORTANT THAT YOU
SCHEDULE A FOLLOW-UP APPOINTMENT AND BE RE-EVALUATED. You should report any new complaints, symptoms, or
remaining problems at that time. IT IS IMPOSSIBLE FOR THE EMERGENCY DEPARTMENT TO RECOGNIZE AND TREAT ALL
ELEMENTS OF INJURY OR ILLNESS IN A SINGLE VISIT.
lf you have been referred to a specialist provider, it means that we believe you may have a condition that requires the expertise of a
specialist. These providers work in partnership with the hospital and have agreed to see referred patients in their office for further
evaluation. KEEP IN MIND THAT THE SPECIALIST HAS HIS/HER OWN OFFICE POLICIES WHICH MAY REQUIRE PROPER
INSURANCE OR PAYMENT UP FRONT BEFORE THE SPECIALIST WILL SEEYOU. It is your responsibility to call the specialist
provider to make an appointment. We do not have the ability to refer patients to specialists/physicians that work with specific insurance
companies.
Please be advised that all financial charges or billing practices are determined by that practice, not the hospital. if your insurance
company requires that you see a specialist from their approved list, it is your responsibility to contact your insurance company to make
those arrangements. It is also your responsibility to follow any other requirements of your insurance company necessary to obtain
coverage for claims submitted.
| hereby acknowledge receipt of these instructions and information above. | understand that | have received Emergency Treatment only,
which is not a substitute for complete medical care and acknowledge that all of my medical problems may not be known, identified, or
treated prior to my release. | understand the need to arrange follow-up care with the provider as indicated. | understand that | should
contact my primary care provider immediately or return to the Emergency Department, if my condition worsens, fails to improve, or new
symptoms appear.

Accession Exam STATUS Exam Date/Time Ordering Provider
07-CT-24-0001712 CT Spine Cervical WO Auth (Verified) 1/25/2024 02:07 EST HART,GREGORY A,
NP-EMR
Reason For Exam
(CT Spine Cervical WO) neck pain after MVC;Trauma
Report
INDICATION: Motor vehicle collision 1/24/2024 - headache, neck pain, left head
pain status post hitting head on window. Additional History: Substance abuse.
Psychiatric problems. Smoker
TECHNIQUE: CT of the brain was performed without contrast. CT of the cervical
spine was performed without intravenous or intrathecal contrast. Sagittal and
coronal reconstructions were generated.
Automated mA/kV exposure control was utilized and patient examination was performed
in strict accordance with principles of ALARA.
RADIATION AMOUNT: 1367 mGy-cm.
COMPARISON: None Available.
FINDINGS:
CT head:
There is no acute intracranial hemorrhage, midline shift, mass effect or
extra-axial fluid collection. Gray-white differentiation is preserved.
Brain volume and ventricular system are within normal limits for age.
The skull base and calvarium are intact. Mucous retention cysts are seen in the
left maxillary sinus. Mild to moderate mucosal thickening is seen in the ethmoid
air cells. Mild mucosal thickening is seen in the right maxillary sinus. The
remaining paranasal sinuses are unremarkable. The visualized orbits, globes, and
mastoid air cells are unremarkable.
CT cervical spine:
The alignment is anatomic. There is no fracture or traumatic subluxation.
The vertebral body heights are well maintained. Disc spaces are preserved. No
significant central canal stenosis is demonstrated. The neural foramina are patent
throughout.
The paravertebral soft tissues are within normal limits. The visualized upper
chest is unremarkable.
IMPRESSION:
No acute intracranial pathology identified.
No evidence of acute cervical spine fracture.

assaull abuse; sexually ansiilied Unesses; pregnancy, birth control domestic abuse of an adult with a disability:
